Having completed this book for you, my children, which is the last of the knowledge in medicine with its completion, and having reached its end in its expositions and its declarations, it seemed to me to complete it for you with this treatise, which is a part of the practice, that is, of surgery, with the hand.
Since the practice of surgery has been neglected in our region and our time, entirely private, until perhaps its knowledge perished, and its trace was severed; and nothing remained of it but small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which have been altered by hands, and errors and hesitations have befallen them, until its purposes were closed and its effectiveness diminished: It seemed to me to revive it by the arrangement of this treatise, according to the manner of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and to present the forms of cautery instruments and other surgical instruments, with the addition of explanations and the acceleration of necessary procedures.
The reason why a good practitioner of surgery with his hand is not found in our time is that the art of medicine is long, and its author must be trained beforehand in the knowledge of anatomy, as Galen described it, until he knows the aids of the limbs, and their forms, and their connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, tendons, and their number and exit points, and of the pulsating and still veins, and the places of their exits.
And therefore Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with a work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
However, we have already spoken of that at the beginning of this book.
Since whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said concerning anatomy cannot avoid falling into error, whereby people are killed; as I have seen many of those who boast about this knowledge without understanding or experience.
This is because I saw a foolish physician cut a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck, and cut some arteries in her neck; therefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed to remove a stone from an old man, and the stone was large. Therefore, he reached it and pulled it out with a piece of bladder. Therefore, the man died on the third day.
And indeed I had already been called to remove it, and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the sick man that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving payment from a certain Duke of our land for medicine, and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him, a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician, in his ignorance, hurried and bound the fracture over the wound with pillows and small splints with strong binding, and did not allow the wound an outlet.
Then he discharged him according to his own desires. Afterwards, he sent him away after a few days, and ordered him not to loosen the binding: and it remained like that until his leg and foot became abscessed and resulted in his destruction.
I was therefore called to him, and I hurried to loosen the binding, and there followed peace, and he escaped his pains.
However, the corruption had already become established in the limb, and I could not restrain it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to spread in the limb until it perished.
And I saw another physician, who pierced the cancerous abscess: and it ulcerated after days, until his illness worsened with its master.
This is because when cancer is pure from melancholic humor, then it is not necessary to reach it with iron at all, unless it be in a limb that can tolerate its being completely severed.
And therefore, children, it is necessary for you to know that surgery is divided into two divisions: namely, surgery with which health is associated; and surgery with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already brought forth in every place of this book, in which surgery comes, in which there is terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of it and to diminish it, so that fools may not find a way to speak ill of it and disgrace it.
Therefore, accept the measure with care and protection, and your sick ones with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading by God's grace to health and praiseworthy success: and leave the terrible illnesses of difficult cure: and remove your souls from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation may enter upon your faith and your benefit.
For it is more remaining to your glory, and more sublime in this world, and finally to your possessions.
For Galen already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat a bad illness, lest you be called a bad doctor.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three chapters.
First chapter.
Concerning the cautery with fire, and cautery with sharp medicine, epitomized and arranged from head to foot, and concerning the forms of instruments, and the implements of the cautery, and everything necessary in the operation.
Second chapter.
Concerning incision and perforation, phlebotomy and cupping, and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things: and all epitomized, arranged by the forms of instruments.
Third chapter.
Concerning restoration, and dislocation, and the treatment of twisting, and similar things: epitomized, arranged from head to foot, and concerning the forms of instruments.
But before I recall the operation with it, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of its benefits and harms, and in what temperament it is to be used.
I say therefore, that the discussion of the quality of the cautery's benefit and harm is a lengthy and subtle discourse, a science and hidden secret.
Many wise men have spoken on this subject, and disagreed on it; and for my part, a little of their words is sufficient, fearing prolixity.
I say therefore, that the cautery benefits every temperament, whether with matter or without matter, except for the two temperaments which are hot without matter, and dry without matter.
However, they disagreed in hot and dry temperament with matter. For some said that the cautery is helpful in it. And others said the opposite, namely that the cautery is not suitable in an illness resulting from heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat, and it is unsuitable that one be healed from a hot and dry illness with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite stated that through the cautery a benefit is achieved in every hot and dry illness that happens in human bodies, because when you compare a human body and its humors to the temperament of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I indeed say through his statement: because by experience it has already revealed that to me several times.
However, it is not fitting that one come upon it, unless one who is already proven and practiced in the final exercise of the cautery chapter, and has known the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and the length of their time.
However, from the remaining complexions there is no fear for you; and especially in cold and humid illnesses. For already all physicians have agreed upon them, and have not disagreed in the benefit of cautery in them.
And know, children, that from the secret of healing through cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine, is this: because fire is simple, whose action does not reach, except the member that is cauterized; and it does not harm another member joined to it, except with little harm.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches that which is distant from the members; and perhaps it causes illness of difficult healing to occur in the member, and perhaps it kills.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it overflows.
However, that has now become known to us through experiment, because of the length of servitude and study with the art, and standing on the truth of things; and because of that I am excused from the length of speech.
And if it were not so, because it is not permitted to this book of mine, I would bring to you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses by a demonstrative philosophical discourse, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree about the time in which the cauterization should be performed, and they place a better time in the spring.
And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, because the harm that is incidental due to the time is submerged in the benefit that is drawn with the cauterization. And especially if the cauterization is for pains from necessary, strong, urgent pains, which do not tolerate delay, because it is feared from them that a greater evil will happen than the small harm which occurs due to the time.
And do not fall into your minds, O children, that which the common people and foolish physicians do not fear, namely that the illness cured by cauterization does not always return.  They consider that a consequence, but it is not as they think; because cauterization is not, unless in place of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries the humidity which is the cause of why the pains occur.
However, cauterization is superior to medicine in its swiftness of health, and the power of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion.  And it is possible for the illness to return at some time according to the complexion of the sick person, and the location of their illness, and its power, and that which is prepared in their body from the aggregation of superfluities in it, and that which comes to them in its acquisition from food, and similar causes, unless it is the illness for which cauterization is administered.
A subtle illness in a limb from few superfluities and humidities, like a toothache, because of the pain, and similar to it, it is possible that that pain will not return in it. But that happens in few cases.
But truly the common people's saying, that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, is a true statement; not in the way they intend it, however, because they believe it is not a cure that compares with medicine, nor with anything after the cauterization has passed.
However, the reality is the opposite of that, and the intention that cauterization is the last resort of medicine is not, except when we administer methods of cure in some illnesses, and those medicines do not help; then we administer cauterization at the end of the matter, and it helps.  Then it follows that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention understood by the common people and many ignorant doctors.
However, the ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say that except because of the equal nature of gold and the excellence of its substance, and they said that the area of the cauterization does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely true, because I have already tested it, and found that it does not do so in some bodies without others.
And cauterization with it [gold] is good, and better than with iron, just as they said. However, when you cauterize with gold in fire, it is not clear to you when it is heated according to the amount you desire, because of the redness of the gold; and when it quickly cools, and if you add further heat to it, it melts in the fire and changes into sheets.
Therefore, the artisan falls from that occupation, and because of that cauterization with iron is faster and more readily available to us, in terms of suitability for the operation.
And indeed I have already ordered this chapter on cauterization, according to chapters, and have arranged them from head to foot, so that they will alleviate the one seeking what he wishes from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization contributes to the dominion of moisture and coldness upon the brain; these two are the causes of headaches, and of a multitude of flows of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and of a multitude of sleep, and toothache, and sore throat; and universally of every illness which arises from coldness, such as paralysis, and headaches, epilepsies, and apoplexies, and similar illnesses to those.
The method of cauterization is that you should instruct the sick person to be evacuated first with a cleansing laxative medicine, cleansing the head for three or four nights, according to what the sick person's strength, age, and custom require.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands in a square position, so that he has already placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the root of your palm upon the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever, therefore, your middle finger shall reach, mark that place with the cautery.
Then apply the olive-shaped cautery to the fire.
Then place it upon the place marked with the cautery, descending, so that your hand is gradually constricted, and you will revolve it. Then quickly lift your hand and look at the place.
If you see now exposed from the bone a quantity of alkiel, or a quantity of zeuherbi, then raise your hand. And if not, repeat your hand with the iron itself, or with another from it if it cools: until the bones, which I said to you, are seen.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cotum in it, and place it over the place, and leave it for three days.
Then place the soaked cotum on butter, and leave it over the place, until the eschar of the fire is destroyed. Then treat it with tetrapharmacon ointment, until it is healed.
Now they have said that the more a wound remains open, the more it discharges pus: therefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized to the bone, and the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of bone is burned.
Then that which has been burned from the bone should be scraped away, then treated.
And others say that it is necessary to reach the utmost with the cautery, until it makes a deep impression on the bone, so that the bone falls away, which happens like a kirate shape: or a tool that women use to prick the small alphabet; and they believe that vapors of the head are expelled from this place, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it is healed.
However, these two kinds of cautery do not seem to me to be at all useful except in certain people according to the way of fear.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better with the health of the patient.
For the head is weakened by the disruption of its natural continuity, as we have testified in other limbs; and especially when the head of the sick person is naturally weak.  And indeed the first kind of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it; therefore operate with it for the health.
Chapter 3.
When chronic pain occurs in the whole head and it is prolonged in the sick person, and he uses leeches, and cupping, and head purges, and oils, and poultices. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the single cautery, which we have described, and none of those things helps it: then consider. For if the head of the sick person is of strong natural constitution, and is not weak, and encounters violent cold, then cauterize with another cautery slightly below the first. Then cauterize the entire area above each horn of his head with a cautery, however, do not penetrate the skin and expose a quantity of bone, as we have described. And cauterize the area on the back of his head, in the location called the *vas*—and it is the place where the cupping vessel is placed—and elevate your cautery there; and do not expose the bone. For the sick person will experience intense pain due to that, differing from the pain of the other cauterizations on the entire head.
And I will say this cautery should be in its place: and it should be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of his head with a finer cautery, than that which cauterizes the middle of the head.
Chapter IV.
When pain and throbbing occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is relieved by medicines that cleanse the head, and the remaining treatment, which I have described in the divisions of illnesses, is not effective, then cauterization is appropriate in two ways: either cauterization with a burning, sharp medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with a burning, sharp medicine is as follows: take one clove of garlic, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then, incise the site of the pain with a broad lancet until a space is made beneath the skin, into which the clove is placed.
Then insert it into the space beneath the skin until it is hidden.  Then tie over it with a suitable constriction of a bandage, and leave it for fifteen hours, then remove it and extract the garlic.  Leave the wound for two or three days, then apply a poultice soaked in butter until the site produces pus; then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, do it with certain burning medicines, which I have written about in the twelfth treatise, on Burning Medicines.
However, its cauterization with iron is according to this method. The cautery iron, whose form is this.
And it is called a nail, because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is something curved, and in its middle is a small protuberance.
Then place it upon the place, and hold your hand; and you should turn the iron slowly with speed; and let the quantity that is burned be from the thickness of the skin, like half of it. And lift your hand, so that the artery, which is below, is not burned, and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak a poultice in salt water, and place it upon the place, and leave it for three days; then place the poultice with butter; afterward, treat with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second cautery's knife-edge. And beware of incision of the artery in this hemicrania, not properly ancient.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in an ancient hemicrania.
When treating hemicrania, using what we have said in the preceding treatment, and what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and if the treatment does not help: and you see from the illness that what we have said regarding the first cautery with medicine, or with cautery with fire, is not sufficient, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery's knife-edge until it whitens, after having marked the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or something similar; and place your hand in one place, and press it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to be careful not to burn the jawbone, which moves during chewing, or the nerve that moves it, lest a spasm result.
And be on guard, and cautious about the flow of blood from the severed artery. For in its severance there is fear, especially for him who does not know what he is doing, and is not studious or experienced; and he abandons the operation at the start.
And I will come with a reminder of the regulation of blood flow arising from the artery in its manner and in its place in this book.
If, however, you see from the sickness that this cautery is not sufficient for him, and you see the body of the sick man tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head, as we have recounted, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery, which we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with a cautery having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
Concerning the method of cauterization in earache.
When earache occurs due to cold, and is treated with solvents, and the remaining treatment which we have described in the division, and the pain is not removed, then cauterize with fire: and that is what is called the Point, whose shape is this.
Then, after its ignition, apply the points along the circumference of the entire ear, as it revolves; or along the circumference of each ear, if the pain is in both simultaneously. And move the cautery slightly away from the root of the ear, after you have marked the places with ink; and let the amount of cautery be ten points on each ear, and like that.
Then treat the places until they heal.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a Torture.
Chapter VII.
Torture that is treated with cauterization is only from those species that arise from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cauterization of the species that arises from desiccation and nerve spasm.
When you treat this species of torture with enemas, and head-cleansings, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the afflicted person with three cauteries: one near the root of the ear, and a second a little lower from its temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery opposite the afflicted part. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with a cautery directly at the tip of the upper ear, just beneath the horn of the head; and another in the temple, whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And hold your hand with the cautery until a quantity equal to half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type from a knife, whose form is previously described; however, it is not a little finer than that, as you see; and it is necessary that the knife have a little excess of thickness in it.
Then care for the places, with what preceded, until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in ancient apoplexy.
When apoplexy is longstanding, and you have treated it with what we have said, and your treatment does not help, and the sick person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries upon each horn of his head, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, as we said, and with a cautery on the back of the head, according to what preceded: and let the method of the cautery be according to what preceded.
Also, he is cauterized with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and it is more of a last resort.
Then, let him be treated with what preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that large hyerae and pills that cleanse the brain be given to the sick person first, in their drink.
Then shave the entire head of the sick person, and place on the back of his head a plaster of the type described in the treatise on plasters concerning sinapis; and apply it repeatedly.
For that is the method of the cautery; and do it according to the same order as I stated there.
If therefore it heals by that, it is good. If not, then make three cauteries on the back part of his head, which shall descend from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye; and place the thickness of a finger between each cautery.
Then treat the cautery with what preceded it.
If however you wish an addition, and the sick person is weak in tolerating it, then make a cautery in the middle. If however you wish an addition, then cauterize him above the two horns.
Then treat him until he is healed; and let the cautery be oily according to the form which was stated previously.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed in cleansing the head with hyæris, and with what we said.
Then shave the head of the sick person; afterward cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery over each horn of the head, and with a cautery over its back, and with three over the vertebrae of the neck.
However, if in the illness there is need for softening the body with more of these, and the sick person is tolerant, and the illness is severe, then cauterize him with four cauteries over the vertebrae of the back, and finally with a cautery, until most of it is burned from the skin, and raise your hand. Then treat him until he is healed; and thus the cautery of Oliuare.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, unless that whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you first cleanse his brain with leeches, and with the rest of the treatment that we have described in the division: when the sick person is strong, or is tolerant in receiving medicines.
If however, it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and cleansing mastications for the brain are administered, many days prior to that, with the improvement of foods.
Then shave his head, afterward cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the manner: and with another cautery on his occiput, and with a cautery on each horn of his head. If, however, the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries that I described in the case of paralysis, and soften the body over the vertebrae of the neck and vertebrae of the back; and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the method that preceded.
If, however, the patient is a child, then apply a thin cautery, according to this method.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries that we mentioned in the case of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is excess of the downward inclination to melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him a drink that will purify his brain, according to what preceded in the division; then shave the patient's head, and afterwards make a neatly fashioned roll of linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head, and the patient, sitting upright, must be held secure on all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is better made from old sheep's butter. And heat it over a fire with a moderate amount of heat, which the finger can tolerate when introduced into it. Then apply it to the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.
Do this to the sick person once a week, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small points on it, holding the hand with the cautery close to it: indeed, let it be by smelling.
For this type of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then place on it a cloth soaked in butter, or chicken fat.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in descending water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you by the signs, which I have said in the division, then begin and let the weak drink it, with that which cleanses his head.
And keep him from all dampness, and make him sit in a bath, fasting for several days.
Then command him to shave his head, and cauterize him in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him above the two temples with two cauteries, if the descent of water is beginning in both eyes simultaneously; or from one side, if the beginning of water is in one eye; and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin; and let the cauteries be long in the width of the temples; and beware of the flow of blood.
If you see anything from it, then cut it immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with the knowledge that is in the extraction of arteries, and the cutting of them, and caution from the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries ultimately produced.
Concerning the method of cauterization in ancient weeping.
When the tears of the eyes are ancient, constant; and are upon the veins and arteries that are in the manifest exterior of the head, it is verified that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities; then cauterize with the same cautery that I have described in the beginning of descending water, with a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck under the two bones. And if it needs addition, then cauterize it on every side of the cavity of the eye, above the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a foul odor of the nose.
When you treat it, with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help; then quickly, and give in a drink to the weak person cochlias three nights; afterwards shave his head, and cauterize it with a middle cautery, with an olive cautery. Then cauterize it with a clavicle cautery, with two cauteries, above the two eyebrows under the hairs a little.
And guard against the artery, lest you strike it.
And this is the form of the Clavilli cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterization in the softening of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this lunate cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on every part; and let them be distant from the two temples; and let the length of each cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not bring your hand with the cautery to the limit, but according to the amount that the third eyelid is to be burned.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the eyelid with hairs reversed, stinging the eye.
The cautery is in it according to two methods: either cautery with fire, or cautery with a burning medicine.
In cautery with fire, beforehand tell the sick person to remove his hairs, if he is one of those who cleanses them, until they are elongated and equalized. If, however, they prick him at their origin, then bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they are born.
When therefore they are born and equalized, then place the sick person's head in your lap; then mark above the eyelids of his eyes with ink, a mark which is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the mark be close to the hairs.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white, or in psyllium mucilage, over the eye.
Then apply a cautery, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the shape that you have marked, gradually in many stages, until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is entirely burned away.
And the sign of the success of your work is, that if you see the eyelid now contracting, and the hairs rising at the puncture of the eye.
Therefore raise your hand then, and leave it for three days.
Then place on it a compress with butter, until the eschar is removed. Then treat it with ointment, until it is healed.
If any hair grows back after an hour, and the eyelid softens: then again cauterize that place, as you did at first.
If however the hairs are in the lower part, then cauterize it, until it is raised to its natural place, and made even so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is that you should instruct the sick person to let the hairs be, until they lengthen and become even. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from paper and cloth.
Then take from known soap, and from unsoaked lime, each one a weight of one ounce, or approximately that: then grind them together thoroughly, and do that quickly, so that it does not cool down. Then, spread some of it from the paste onto the paper you have made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid of one or two eyes. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in egg white: and let the head of the sick person be in your bosom.
And place your index finger on the medicine, and press it for a little while. And you should move it whenever the sick person feels the medicine's bite, because its bite is found to be like fire.
While, therefore, this that he finds, the bite, lasts, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. When therefore the bite ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid raise, as it raises with a contraction from fire, or with an incision, it is well; and if not, then again put some medicine onto the place where the medicine does not take effect, and does not darken, until your operation is equalized, and the eye contracts.
Then place on it Cotum with butter, until the skin of the burn is eradicated. Then treat it with diaphinicon ointment, or another, until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to maintain the utmost care, so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after days, and something from the hair fights its way into the eye, then apply medicine again to the place on the eyelid that is softening, as you did at first. Then treat it until it heals.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be; and the way of rectitude is not hidden from him who is diligent in this art.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a tear duct fistula.
When you treat a fistula, in the same way as we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then, it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Command the sick person to place his head in your lap, and let the attendant hold his head between his hands in such a way that it does not move or shake with his head.
Then place a cautery, soaked in egg white or in psyllium mucilage, over his eye; then apply the cautery, whose shape is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's wing feather from one end, with which the cautery is made; and if you wish, it may extend penetratingly to the other end, and if you wish, it may be held upward in this way.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and extract the pus from it and dry it; and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place the cautery, which is made very hot, upon it.
And hold your hand with the cautery near the eye, towards the nose, so that your hand does not wander or the sick person is not disturbed; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and corrupt it.
If therefore you reach in the beginning of your cautery's application up to the bone, it will be well. And if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need it, and leave it for three days.
Then place a cloth with butter, and care for it with a drying ointment, until it is healed.
If forty days have passed and it is not healed, then place upon it a sharp, corrosive medicine, until the bone is exposed; and scrape it according to what is coming in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing fistulas, which some of the first [authors] said. Direct your attention to the location of the fistula, and split it open; then place in the fissure a fine camahan, that is, a fine cannula, whose shape is this. And pour into it a drachma of melted lead, and hold your hand with the cannula firmly, and let the sick person not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run, or reach his eye.
And it is necessary that you place over the sick person's eye a poultice steeped in egg white, or in water.
For lead burns the area of the fistula, and heals it with a marvelous cure.
If the fistula is healed by what we have said concerning the cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a nasal passage, and to reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come to its own proper place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in lip fissures.
Often fissures occur in the lip, called hairs, and especially in the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures, with what we have said in the division of illnesses, and if treatment does not help, then cauterize with a small knife cautery, according to this form.
And its concavity should be according to the sharpness of the knife.
Then quickly place it, heated, on the fissures themselves, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a cautery, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth; then it produces pus, and bursts; afterward it becomes chronic, and pus flows, and a fistula forms; then you treat it, and treatment is of no avail, then it is necessary to cauterize the fistula with a cautery of a size that matches it. Then introduce the heated iron into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches its depth and its end; do this once, or twice.
Then treat it afterwards, with what we have said about treatment until it is healed.
If, therefore, the pus is cut off and healed, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place, and remove the corrupted bone according to what will be found in its head.
Concerning the method of cauterization in softened gums and teeth.
When the gum softens because of moisture, and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not help: then place the head of the sick person in your bosom.
Then, with fire, a cautery, whose form will come after this, so that you place the Cannula over the tooth: and quickly insert into it the heated Cautery: and hold your hand for a little while, until the sick person feels the heat of the fire already reaching the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand; then repeat the cautery several times, according to what you wish.
Then let the sick person fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour, and spit it out.
For the moved tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupt moisture is dried.
Concerning the method of cauterizing toothache.
When toothache is due to cold, either the tooth itself is cold, or there is a worm, and treatment with medicines does not help, then the cautery is applied to it in two ways: either cautery with butter, or cautery with fire.
However, cautery with butter is as follows: take cow's butter and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a pan. Then take a cotton swab and wrap it around the tip of the probe. Then immerse it in the boiled butter and quickly place it on the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools; then repeat it several times, until the fire's effect reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or cotton in cold butter and place it on the aching tooth, and place a heated iron on top of it, until the fire reaches the deep cavity of the tooth.
Its cauterization with fire is as follows: apply a brass or iron cannula. And let there be something of its thickness in its body so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the sick person's bone.
Then take a cautery, whose form will be shown, and place it on that tooth, and hold your hand until the cautery cools down.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or on another day.
And it is necessary, in the application of that cautery, that the sick person fill their mouth with good butter and hold it for one hour; then let them spit it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever extremity of force is possible; and this is the form of the cannula.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Strophulus.
When Strophulus are from phlegm and from cold humors, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, and force hastens their digestion, then with a concave cautery of fire, whose form is this.
Having two open extremities, so that smoke may escape from the cautery at one extremity; and place it ignited upon the abscess once, and a second time, if need be, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
If the abscess is small, then place the cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a poultice infused in butter, until that which the fire burned is removed.
Then treat it with tooth ointment, until the form of the cannula is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When moistures overcome the lung passage, and especially when it is with a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the infirm person be evacuated first with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it at the root of the throat in the depressed place, and beware, lest you reach the throat with the cauter, nor the skin, unless something of it.
Then cauterize it with another cauter at the junction of the neck at the last vertebra of it, finishing: and let the cauter be narrow according to the manner which preceded.
Then treat it with what preceded until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in diseases of the lung, and cough.
When cough and disease of the lung are from cold humors, and the sick person does not have fever, nor consumption, and the disease is old, then cauterize him with two cauteries above the fork in low, smooth, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be of a tube according to the form that preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by puncturing with a cautery, called Point, whose form preceded in puncturing the pain of the ears: and let the punctures be from thirty points up to as many more.
Then treat him with what preceded, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore, the cauterization will be alleviated when you do it with three cauteries at one time.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the assisting cause of humidities is dislocated, and is not fixed at the time of its return from its dislocation, until such time as it is accustomed to returning, then it is dislocated by a slight movement, which happens as we have already testified it, then it is necessary to reduce the dislocation first. Then the sick person shall be placed on their back, or on their healthy side. Then raise the skin that is in the inner titillico upwards with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is dislocated inwards.
Then taking a cautery with two prongs. Whose shape is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the shape of the cauterization will be with four cauteries.
And sometimes a cauterization is made with a cautery having three prongs, therefore the shape of the cauterization is then six cauteries: and the prongs are according to the thinness of the thread.
And this is the shape of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added to this shape, therefore there are eight cauteries.
Then place crushed leeks with salt on the cautery. Then cause the infirm person to adhere to stillness, so that the limb is not moved at any time until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is upwards, and that rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a hooked cautery, or with many cauteries by pricking.
For the joint is strengthened, and moisture is removed: and the infirm person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When there are cold and many moistures in the stomach, until they extract it from its complexion, and the catarrhs multiply in it, and frequent modes of treatment, and do not benefit: then it is necessary that the infirm person be laid on their back, and extend their legs, and their hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, one cautery beneath the spoon-shaped region of the chest, a finger's breadth in size, with a cautery like a nail, and two cauteries below from two sides of the single cautery, until the shape of the cauteries becomes triangular. And lengthen between each so that they do not join, when they will make pus.
And the depth of the cautery should be the amount of two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form, without addition; and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach, according to this form, let the cautery by which this is done be single, in the form of a circle, according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking him who is terrified by this cautery; and it is, as if signs on the stomach a point according to the amount, which you wish with ink; then cauterize it with the cautery of the point; then treat it with the treatment which preceded until it is healed.
Of the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When pain occurs in the liver from coldness and moisture, or from thick windiness, until it emerges from its natural complexion by superfluous discharge, and the sick person is treated with what we have said, and it does not benefit him: then it is necessary that the sick person be placed supine on his neck, and mark with ink three cauteries according to this figure, and this same amount, on the lower liver from the hypochondria, where the human elbow reaches; and let the space between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body; and do not press your hand with the cautery much.
And let the amount of what is burned be, from the thickness of the skin, the amount of half of it, not added; and let the sick person be standing on his feet.
If however, he is not standing, then let him be lying down, who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you, to cauterize these cauteries with a knife cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And guard yourself, so that you do not proceed to the utmost in cauterization, and the thickness of the entire skin is burned, wherefore the whole body is burned, and reaches the intestines: because the skin there is thin, therefore know that.
Concerning the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When an issue occurs, and you wish to know if that abscess is in the flesh of the liver, or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the sick person is afflicted by pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the tunic of the liver, there is intense sharpness with the pain: and you already see that the treatment has fatigued its physicians.
Therefore, it is necessary that the sick person lie on their back. Then mark the location of the abscess with ink; then apply a cautery heated like a sunbeam. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery, until the whole skin is burned and it reaches the pus, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with the treatment for issues, until it is healed.
And it is not necessary for one to use this type of cautery unless one's study in the art of medicine is prolonged, and through whose hands such illnesses have come together with experience several times; then indeed let one dare to undertake such an operation.
But truly, to leave it is better, in my opinion.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Pleuritis.
The ancients said that cautery with aristolochia roots is for cold pleurisy according to this method. And it is that you take from the dry long aristolochia roots, one root longer than the others, and of the thickness of a finger. Then immerse it in oil, and light it in fire. Then cauterize with one cautery in that which is between the continuation of the fork with the neck, and with two small cauteries slightly sloping downwards to the part below the beard.
And with two cauteries also in that which is between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping slightly backwards; and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from behind: one in that which is between the two shoulder blades; and with two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, below the cautery that is between the two shoulder blades.
And you should not press your hand with the cautery, but rather it should be evident by smelling the skin.
And some ancient ones have said that there are people who use a cautery of iron similar to a rod; and they burn, and introduce it into that which is between the ribs, until they reach with it the abscess itself, and the pus comes out; as we have said regarding the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is fear, that either the weak person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, which has no cure.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Spleen, Chapter XXXII.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, with what we have said regarding the treatment in the division of illnesses, and if your treatment does not help, then the cautery is used in it according to three methods, all of which are correct.
One of which is to make three cauteries, or four, drawing lines along the length of the spleen according to the figure of the cauteries of the liver, of which the figure preceded.
And let there be between each cautery a quantity equal to the thickness of a finger, or a little more or less.
And let the method of the cautery be, which we said in the cautery of the liver, equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the infirm person lie supine on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: that you heat the cautery having two points, which we said in the chapter on the dislocation of the humerus: and raise the skin, which is in a direct line with the spleen, where the left elbow of the infirm person reaches: and let your lifting be such that you lift the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then introduce two very hot points, until with them you penetrate the skin on the other side; then withdraw the cautery; thus, four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery having three points.
Then treat the cautery after you have dismissed it to emit pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than any of the preceding cures.
Concerning the method of cauterization in dropsy.
The cautery does not fall on dropsy, unless properly applied.
When you treat a dropsical patient with the methods of treatment we have mentioned in the division, and the treatment is not effective, then you must cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and with one cautery on the stomach, and another on the liver, and one on the spleen, and with two cauteries after the back between the vertebrae, and one in the direct line of the chest, and another in the direct line of the stomach: and let the depth of the cautery be approximately equal to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open, that it may discharge pus for a long time.
And do not remove the sick person from treatment after the cautery with him; because it is necessary that two intentions be gathered in him; and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The shape of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized should be a nail, according to its previous shape; and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to its previous shape.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When boils fester in a dropsy patient, and are filled with yellow water, you should cauterize on the back of the foot, in the nocrati, which is between the auricular and annular areas; and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it; then raise your hand; and do not repeat it at all.
For the yellow water will sweat out, and the cautery should be of this form.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be with the sharp end of the cautery; and let the cautery be along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other below that, approximately in the middle of the leg; and make two cauteries on each thigh; and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time, so that some water may sweat out from it; then treat it with the rest of what we have said.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in abdominal ailment.
Chapter 35.
When the abdominal ailment is from cold and dampness, weakening the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines, and it is treated by methods of cure but does not heal; and you see the sick person tolerating a cautery of exuberant strength, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, as was previously done in cauterizing the stomach with a circular cautery, and four small cauteries around the navel, with a small claw-like cautery; and a large cautery on the lower back, or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moisture, and the sick person tolerates it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the ribs, and a cautery on each hip; and perhaps add two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach.
For it is a beneficial cure, whose aid does not err.
Concerning the method of cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When in the anus there are many old hemorrhoids, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted moisture, and they are treated with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower spinal column of the back, under the almeidati somewhat triangularly, and a cautery under the navel, as if by two fingers' width.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face becoming pustular, then cauterize him on his stomach with a large cautery, according to what preceded: and cauterize on his liver, and another on his spleen, with a clauili cautery: and leave the cautery open for a time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you excise althelul, then cauterize with a cautery that resembles a ray. Then insert it [the heated cautery] into the excised althelul: and with the last of your hand, until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, from which blood flows: do this once, or twice.
If therefore the althelul are many, then cauterize each one with the cautery according to what we have narrated. Then treat them with what benefits them from the ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over alcatin, it is more beneficial in the end.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the patient does not obey the incision and the operation that we have described in its place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he is healed with a cautery.
When therefore a fistula occurs to someone, and becomes chronic, pus runs from it, and corrupt humours. Therefore it is more fitting that you probe it with a slender probe. Then ascertain its depth with the probe.
Then heat the cautery, which is similar to a ray. Then introduce the heated cautery into the fistula itself, and note the quantity in which the cautery entered.
And repeatedly apply the cautery to it until all those corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to your necessity.
And guard yourself from burning the nerve, if there is one there, or a large vein; or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then guard yourself from all these locations.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy location and you judge it not to be penetrating.
Then treat the location until it is healed.
If however the location is sealed, and the materials are cut away from it, and it remains like this for a long time, then know that it is now healed completely.
And if they do not cut away the materials from it, then know that it is penetrating, or a corrupt bone is in its depth, or something like that from those things; whose mention will come in its place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Kidneys.
When pain in the kidneys occurs from cold or from strong wind, and it diminishes thereby the strength of the afflicted person, then it is necessary to cauterize it above the almethen, above the kidneys themselves, with a cautery on every kidney with a nail cautery, whose mention preceded.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time on the almeidatu itself. Therefore three lines will appear. Therefore the latter will be more helpful.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening of the bladder occur from cold and moisture, so that the afflicted person cannot retain urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the summit above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin.  Cauterize from the right side of the summit, and from the left side of it, and let the length of the cauterization on either side be according to the size of a thumb's breadth. And cauterize it with a cautery from the lower back, or with two cauteries if you need them, and let it be according to the previous cautery's closure.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the uterus.
When cold and moisture affect the uterus, hindering impregnation, corrupting her menstrual flow, delaying its discharge, and causing pain during its arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in cauterizing the bladder, and with a cautery above the lower back, or with two cauteries: and let the cautery be closed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When mucous humours discharge into the anus and cause its exit from its proper place; and a sign of this is that one leg is extended over the other when compared, and the place of the dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore, it is necessary to cauterize the affected area above the anus itself with a similar circular cautery, after marking the circumference of the anus with ink as it revolves, so that the anus itself falls within the centre of the circle.
If this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, using a large olive-shaped cautery; and let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin overall.
Then treat it until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and moisture; and the patient is treated with what we have mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not help, and it becomes chronic: then it is necessary to free the patient from gross humours with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar remedies. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cauterization in it is according to two methods: either cauterization with burning medicines, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with fire is according to many methods.
One of them is to cauterize over the hip joint itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this shape. And make them a good or bad depth. And let the space between each cautery be the thickness of a finger; let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is made in the middle over the head of the hip itself. Therefore, there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip, one: so that the circle contain the entire hip.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery in sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If however it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the thigh, over the place to which the sick person points there, where the pain is, and with your cautery on the calf four fingers to the wild side for a little while: and let the cautery be a knife-like one.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
If the sick person indicates that the pain extends to near the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a puncturing cautery, three, or four, or more, if he needs it.
And if he indicates pain to be below the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with one knife-like cautery.
And beware in all your cauterizations, that you do not proceed with the cautery to the point of burning a nerve, or a major artery, and thereby bring upon the sick person a great harm, or contraction.
And indeed I have already seen one and another, of those who have cauterized above the ankle, and have proceeded too far in their cauterization, and the leg has swollen, until the swelling reached the foot, and the whole foot was perforated and corrupted; then there followed a rupture of the belly, and death after that.
If the pain is in two parts simultaneously, cauterize each according to this method.
And some wise men have said in the cauterization of the buttock, whose cautery this is the method. Make a similar cautery of iron, whose diameter is half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a date stone, or a little less: and within that cautery let there be a third cautery.
And let the space that is between each cautery be the size of a thumb's knot: and let the cauteries be open on both sides: and let their height be like a knot, or two knots: and make for them a handle of iron fitting well into the cauteries.
Then it should be heated in fire until it glows red and throws off sparks; then it should be placed upon the affected buttock of the patient lying on his healthy side. Therefore cauterize him with three round cauteries in a single turn.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply plasters with butter, and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasis says, with this kind of cautery, my children, we have used it little, because of the terror of its appearance, and because we find few who wait upon it.
However, it is a good cautery for him who suffers, and finds its place with him.
A cautery, however, is made with burning medicines, so that you make two samia having a perforated armilla, into which descends the hinge of its door, made of bronze or iron, the length of the wall; on whose height they should have two knots, or similar to them.
And let the space between each be the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above, and let them hold each other together in this form.
Then place it on a box of ashes, the sick person lying on their healthy side. And press your hand firmly on the box of ashes. Then pour between the two circles hot water, which has been warmed with fire for a short time, and hold it for a quantity of an hour's time; and let the sick person endure its burning, and its cauterization, for he finds the burning like fire, until the burning subsides.
Then raise your hand with the instrument and wash away the hot water from the entire ash with fresh water; then leave it for three days.
And place butter on it, until the blackness of the burning is removed; and leave it for a few days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the final help.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a poultice on it, containing water, in the same way as you did for the ash.
And this is the method of hot water; and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, each one part: grind both, and place them in a new pot, whose lower part has a single small hole, according to the quantity that the radius will enter: and place another glass pot beneath the bottom of the pot: and pour over the alkali and lime clear water, so that both are submerged by a finger's breadth; then press them with your hand by pressing well; and leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower part of the glass pot.
Then collect all that water and pour it over more lime; and strain it until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong and sharp, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of other limbs. Because it produces the operation of fire itself.
And from medicines are those with which the ankhs are cauterized, also like tesisie, and honey of the anacardi, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed together.
And Galen himself, recounting, reported the cure of a certain man from the ancients, by which the pain of the ankh and sciatic vein was cured: and he magnified that it was very great. And he said, because he did not need any other cure, and because he was healed in one instance, until he reported, that perhaps he had entered a bath carried, and exited from it already healthy.
And it is to be taken from green seitaragi: and if green is not found, take dry, fresh: and it is to be ground a lot with some fat, and placed upon the ankh, where the pain is, or the leg, or in the thigh: and it is to be bound, and left for a quantity of three hours, or for the quantity that the infirm person feels a calming of the burning. Then put him into the bath.
When therefore his body is made moist, put him into a chair. For the pain recedes, and he is healed.
And know that it is not necessary for someone to use a cautery with these remedies unless after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides, who also said that goat dung, when cauterized with it the sciatic vein, helps it: and the cautery is done in this way. Let wool be taken and soaked in old oil, and placed on the deep place, which is between the big toe and the sole, and is closer to the sole.
Then take dry goat dung, and burn it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool, and let it be until it is extinguished. Then repeat it. Therefore do not cease to do that, until feeling comes to the middle, down to the ankle, and the pain rests.
And this method of cautery is called the Vaccinum cautery.
Concerning the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain in the back occurs from many causes, either from an accident, or a blow, or an evacuation of superfluities, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and damp material: and indeed the cautery does not apply, except in this sole case, which is done from the infusion of cold material.
Therefore, after the patient's evacuation with foul pills, and similar things, let three lines be made on the back, where the pain is, according to the width of the afflicted area itself, after marking with ink five cauteries on each line, or more according to the amount tolerated by the patient's strength: and let the cauterization be performed with a pointed cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries, with a middle-clawed cautery, according to this form.
Concerning the method of cauterization in the beginning stages of a humpback.
This illness often happens to young infants.
And the sign of its beginning in children is: that a constriction occurs in their breathing upon elevation and movement; and you find at the lower part of the dorsal spine and its joints, that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see it, and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is circular in this shape.
And let the cautery cover the entire area of the vertebra equally; and if you wish to cauterize the circumference of the vertebra with a pointed cautery, make two or three lines of points, and let the points be close together.
Then treat the location until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, that you do not apply the cautery to the hump, which is formed by the spasm of the nerve.
Concerning the method of cauterization in gout and joint pains.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humors, which are poured forth to any member of the body, then when the pains occur in the feet, it is customary for physicians to name it gout properly.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of cure, and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is that you cauterize it after evacuation, around the joint of the feet, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
And if you need to puncture on the surface of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees, or other joints, and that often happens, then cauterize it above each knee with three or four cauteries on all sides, with this same claw-shaped cautery.
If, however, more cauteries with this cautery are needed, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, but rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If, however, the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what we have said concerning the cautery in its chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, then puncture in a circular pattern around the foci, as if two lines revolved.
If, however, pain remains in the fingers, then puncture them, above every knot, and above the palm of the hand.
If, however, the pains ascend after days to the elbows, or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every side.
And do not evacuate the sick person from a good regimen, from the reception of medicines. For if a good regimen is made, and phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the help of God by this cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine, or the scrotum, descends to the testicle, and that it is beginning to approach it: then it is necessary that you order the sick person to cease eating on his/her day. And that he/she uses from the lenients, so that excrement descends from his/her belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back, and order him to hold his breath until it emerges, or the scrotum, or intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with ink under the rupture over the pubic bone, with a mark whose extremity is similar to half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then cauterize with a cautery, whose form this is, until it becomes white and throws off sparks. Then reduce the intestine, or scrotum, to its concavity. Then let the attendant place his hand on the place so that the intestine does not come out: and you have now opened between the legs of the sick person, and placed a cushion beneath him, and another servant on his legs, and another on his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on that mark, your hand holding the cautery straight. And hold it until you meet with it the mouth; or again with it another time, if you have not met with it at the mouth the first time.
And prudently observe the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it, and death or great harm befall the sick person through it.
And know that when you do not meet with the cautery the mouth, your operation is of no benefit.
And the cautery for children should be fine, according to their measure.
Then treat with the remaining ointments, until it is healed.
And let the sick person lie on their back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you put nourishment for the duration of his healing, which will ease his stomach, so that his intestines do not exit with straining and evacuation.
Then, when he wants to rise after forty days, then administer a properly made bandage, and let him keep it for another forty days.
And lessen his labor, and the fullness of food and drink, and loud voices.
For when he uses this regimen, he is thus healed with complete healing.
And I will speak of the treatment of Ruptures with incision in his chapter.
When, however, Ruptures occur in the rest of the belly, and are incipient, and there is a will that they not increase, then cauterize the Rupture with a round cautery according to its quantity; and let that which is seared from then on be like a third of it. Then treat him with what we have said, and it will not increase.
And some early ones have already said that the Rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this shape.
After it is marked with ink, and a line is placed which is through the width in the upper side of the Rupture, and another line to the lower one. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery tongs.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterization in pains due to a fall or a blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When in certain limbs pain arises from a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of every limb be a cautery according to its size, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twisting, and the pain from it.
If therefore it is healed by the first cautery, it is well. If not, then repeat the cautery upon it.
Because it is customary for these pains to shift from one limb to the one next to it. Therefore, it is necessary to pursue them with cautery until the infirmity is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Leprosy.
Leprosy patients are sometimes greatly helped by cauterization. And especially the type of leprosy that arises from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: therefore, when you wish to cauterize it, consider that.
If therefore the leprosy is stubborn, and you have treated it with what we have said in the division, and it does not descend, nor does it stand; and you fear for the sick person that corruption will encompass his entire constitution: then cauterize him on his head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head known, and a second below it toward the forehead at the end of the hair, and two upon the two horns, and one behind upon the nape of the neck.
And hold your hand with the cautery for a little while, until it makes a small impression on the orifice, and the cortices are loosened from it: so that the expiration of gross vapors from it may be relieved, and cauterize with the cautery also upon the spleen itself, according to what has gone before.
But if the leprosy is already spread over the sick person, and appears manifestly: then it is necessary that you cauterize with those cauteries which we have said for the head, and with a cautery on the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries on the two jaws, and with two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and with six on the vertebrae of the back, and with one large one on the haunches near the tail and one above it, on the very buttock; and with two on the thighs: namely, one on each thigh, and with two on the knees: one on each knee, and with two on the shoulders, and with two on the elbows, and with two on the soft parts of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of his fingers of his hands and feet: and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and the knuckles of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, so that you do not burn them.
And sometimes a cautery is applied to the sternum, and another to the stomach, and another to the liver.
And know that the more you add cautery, the more help and benefit there is.
And know that the sick person does not find pain in the cautery, as healthy people do, because his body is already numb.
And there should be cauteries of large and small size, according to the limbs and joints, as has been previously described in the types of instruments.
Then treat the cautery with herb flour and honey, and with other remedies until healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a state of numbness.
When any limb is numb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then cauterize that numb limb with cauteries, according to the size of the limb, whether large or small.
And let your cautery penetrate the skin a little. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized for some numbness that occurs in the hand and foot, in the vertebrae of the back at the exit of the nerves that move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
But let no one presume upon it unless he is wise in the anatomy of the limbs and the exit of the nerves that move the body.
Chapter LI.
When Albaras is old and nothing from the arts of medicine is of use in it, then cauterize over it itself with a deep cautery for a short while, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with flour of herbs, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and dove's blood, and swallow's blood; of each, take one part; mix these things together, and apply them to a cloth, and let them adhere to the place until it is healed.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing in Cancer.
When the Cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, just as it revolves.
Wise men, however, said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
However, it does not seem right to me, because I fear that it will ulcerate: and I have already seen that happen several times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Adubelati.
When someone has Adubelati, and it is delayed in maturation, either because of excess causing it, or because of the patient's age, when they are feeble with little blood, or because of the time, and the need to hasten the maturation of Adubelati, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by puncturing. Then leave it. For it will hasten with maturation.
If however you wish to perforate it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, whose form is this.
And place it in the middle of the Adubelati, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from the one following the sick person, so that the course of pus may be alleviated.
Then treat it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a corroding evil.
Chapter LIII.
A corroding thing is nothing other than corruption walking in a limb, and it corrodes it; just as fire consumes dry wood.
If therefore you see a corroding thing in a place that can tolerate a cautery with fire, then apply many cauteries of fire, small and large iron cauteries, according to what is suitable to the place where the corroding thing is.
Then cauterize it from every side until you eradicate the entire corruption, and nothing of it remains at all.
Then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places powdered sulfur with oil, until all the eschars and all corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days healthy flesh is born, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then repeat the cautery on whatever remains of the corrupted places.
And it is sometimes cured by corroding medicine. For it itself arises in the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of quicker benefit; and indeed I have already said that cauterization with sharp medicine is in division; therefore, take it there when you need it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in corns and warts.
Chapter LV.
This ailment frequently occurs in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a thick, filtered thing that hurts the foot.
And cautery in them is indeed according to two methods: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for cautery with fire, you should heat a concave cautery similar to a vulture's wing, made of iron, according to the size that encompasses the corn on all sides, and have thin edges.
Then place it, heated, upon the corn. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the corn, until the cautery reaches the depth of the corn, and leave it for three days, until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply a plaster to it with crushed wild herbs and salt, and leave the plaster on it overnight. For it will be eradicated from its roots.
Then treat the area with a generative flesh ointment, until it is healed.
If they are not transformed, and often occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet, then apply a cautery to them with hot water.
